<p class="line" name=2.1.280>Which, by the right and virtue of my place,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.281>I ought to know of: and, upon my knees,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.282>I charm you, by my once-commended beauty,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.283>By all your vows of love and that great vow</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.284>Which did incorporate and make us one,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.285>That you unfold to me, yourself, your half,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.286>Why you are heavy, and what men to-night</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.287>Have had to resort to you: for here have been</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.288>Some six or seven, who did hide their faces</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.289>Even from darkness.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.290>Kneel not, gentle Portia.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.291>I should not need, if you were gentle Brutus.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.292>Within the bond of marriage, tell me, Brutus,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.293>Is it excepted I should know no secrets</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.294>That appertain to you? Am I yourself</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.295>But, as it were, in sort or limitation,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.296>To keep with you at meals, comfort your bed,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.297>And talk to you sometimes? Dwell I but in the suburbs</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.298>Of your good pleasure? If it be no more,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.299>Portia is Brutus' harlot, not his wife.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.300>You are my true and honourable wife,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.301>As dear to me as are the ruddy drops</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.302>That visit my sad heart</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.303>If this were true, then should I know this secret.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.304>I grant I am a woman; but withal</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.305>A woman that Lord Brutus took to wife:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.306>I grant I am a woman; but withal</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.307>A woman well-reputed, Cato's daughter.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.308>Think you I am no stronger than my sex,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.309>Being so father'd and so husbanded?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.310>Tell me your counsels, I will not disclose 'em:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.311>I have made strong proof of my constancy,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.312>Giving myself a voluntary wound</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.313>Here, in the thigh: can I bear that with patience.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.314>And not my husband's secrets?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.315>O ye gods,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.316>Render me worthy of this noble wife!</p>
<p><i>Knocking within</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.317>Hark, hark! one knocks: Portia, go in awhile;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.318>And by and by thy bosom shall partake</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.319>The secrets of my heart.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.320>All my engagements I will construe to thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.321>All the charactery of my sad brows:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.322>Leave me with haste.</p>
<p><i>Exit PORTIA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.323>Lucius, who's that knocks?</p>
<p><i>Re-enter LUCIUS with LIGARIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.324>He is a sick man that would speak with you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.325>Caius Ligarius, that Metellus spake of.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.326>Boy, stand aside. Caius Ligarius! how?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>LIGARIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.327>Vouchsafe good morrow from a feeble tongue.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.328>O, what a time have you chose out, brave Caius,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.329>To wear a kerchief! Would you were not sick!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>LIGARIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.330>I am not sick, if Brutus have in hand</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.331>Any exploit worthy the name of honour.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.332>Such an exploit have I in hand, Ligarius,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.333>Had you a healthful ear to hear of it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>LIGARIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.334>By all the gods that Romans bow before,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.335>I here discard my sickness! Soul of Rome!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.336>Brave son, derived from honourable loins!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.337>Thou, like an exorcist, hast conjured up</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.338>My mortified spirit. Now bid me run,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.339>And I will strive with things impossible;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.340>Yea, get the better of them. What's to do?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.341>A piece of work that will make sick men whole.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>LIGARIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.342>But are not some whole that we must make sick?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.343>That must we also. What it is, my Caius,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.344>I shall unfold to thee, as we are going</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.345>To whom it must be done.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>LIGARIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.346>Set on your foot,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.347>And with a heart new-fired I follow you,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.348>To do I know not what: but it sufficeth</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.349>That Brutus leads me on.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.350>Follow me, then.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. CAESAR's house.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Thunder and lightning. Enter CAESAR, in his night-gown</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.1>Nor heaven nor earth have been at peace to-night:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.2>Thrice hath Calpurnia in her sleep cried out,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.3>'Help, ho! they murder Caesar!' Who's within?</p>
<p><i>Enter a Servant</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.4>My lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.5>Go bid the priests do present sacrifice</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.6>And bring me their opinions of success.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.7>I will, my lord.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<p><i>Enter CALPURNIA</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CALPURNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.8>What mean you, Caesar? think you to walk forth?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.9>You shall not stir out of your house to-day.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.10>Caesar shall forth: the things that threaten'd me</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.11>Ne'er look'd but on my back; when they shall see</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.12>The face of Caesar, they are vanished.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CALPURNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.13>Caesar, I never stood on ceremonies,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.14>Yet now they fright me. There is one within,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.15>Besides the things that we have heard and seen,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.16>Recounts most horrid sights seen by the watch.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.17>A lioness hath whelped in the streets;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.18>And graves have yawn'd, and yielded up their dead;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.19>Fierce fiery warriors fought upon the clouds,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.20>In ranks and squadrons and right form of war,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.21>Which drizzled blood upon the Capitol;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.22>The noise of battle hurtled in the air,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.23>Horses did neigh, and dying men did groan,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.24>And ghosts did shriek and squeal about the streets.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.25>O Caesar! these things are beyond all use,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.26>And I do fear them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.27>What can be avoided</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.28>Whose end is purposed by the mighty gods?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.29>Yet Caesar shall go forth; for these predictions</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.30>Are to the world in general as to Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CALPURNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.31>When beggars die, there are no comets seen;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.32>The heavens themselves blaze forth the death of princes.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.33>Cowards die many times before their deaths;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.34>The valiant never taste of death but once.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.35>Of all the wonders that I yet have heard.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.36>It seems to me most strange that men should fear;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.37>Seeing that death, a necessary end,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.38>Will come when it will come.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter Servant</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.39>What say the augurers?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.40>They would not have you to stir forth to-day.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.41>Plucking the entrails of an offering forth,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.42>They could not find a heart within the beast.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.43>The gods do this in shame of cowardice:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.44>Caesar should be a beast without a heart,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.45>If he should stay at home to-day for fear.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.46>No, Caesar shall not: danger knows full well</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.47>That Caesar is more dangerous than he:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.48>We are two lions litter'd in one day,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.49>And I the elder and more terrible:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.50>And Caesar shall go forth.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>CALPURNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.51>Alas, my lord,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.52>Your wisdom is consumed in confidence.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.53>Do not go forth to-day: call it my fear</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.54>That keeps you in the house, and not your own.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.55>We'll send Mark Antony to the senate-house:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.56>And he shall say you are not well to-day:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.57>Let me, upon my knee, prevail in this.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.58>Mark Antony shall say I am not well,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.59>And, for thy humour, I will stay at home.</p>
<p><i>Enter DECIUS BRUTUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.60>Here's Decius Brutus, he shall tell them so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>DECIUS BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.61>Caesar, all hail! good morrow, worthy Caesar:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.62>I come to fetch you to the senate-house.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.63>And you are come in very happy time,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.64>To bear my greeting to the senators</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.65>And tell them that I will not come to-day:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.66>Cannot, is false, and that I dare not, falser:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.67>I will not come to-day: tell them so, Decius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CALPURNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.68>Say he is sick.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.69>                  Shall Caesar send a lie?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.70>Have I in conquest stretch'd mine arm so far,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.71>To be afraid to tell graybeards the truth?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.72>Decius, go tell them Caesar will not come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>DECIUS BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.73>Most mighty Caesar, let me know some cause,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.74>Lest I be laugh'd at when I tell them so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.75>The cause is in my will: I will not come;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.76>That is enough to satisfy the senate.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.77>But for your private satisfaction,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.78>Because I love you, I will let you know:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.79>Calpurnia here, my wife, stays me at home:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.80>She dreamt to-night she saw my statua,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.81>Which, like a fountain with an hundred spouts,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.82>Did run pure blood: and many lusty Romans</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.83>Came smiling, and did bathe their hands in it:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.84>And these does she apply for warnings, and portents,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.85>And evils imminent; and on her knee</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.86>Hath begg'd that I will stay at home to-day.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>DECIUS BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.87>This dream is all amiss interpreted;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.88>It was a vision fair and fortunate:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.89>Your statue spouting blood in many pipes,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.90>In which so many smiling Romans bathed,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.91>Signifies that from you great Rome shall suck</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.92>Reviving blood, and that great men shall press</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.93>For tinctures, stains, relics and cognizance.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.94>This by Calpurnia's dream is signified.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.95>And this way have you well expounded it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>DECIUS BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.96>I have, when you have heard what I can say:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.97>And know it now: the senate have concluded</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.98>To give this day a crown to mighty Caesar.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.99>If you shall send them word you will not come,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.100>Their minds may change. Besides, it were a mock</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.101>Apt to be render'd, for some one to say</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.102>'Break up the senate till another time,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.103>When Caesar's wife shall meet with better dreams.'</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.104>If Caesar hide himself, shall they not whisper</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.105>'Lo, Caesar is afraid'?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.106>Pardon me, Caesar; for my dear dear love</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.107>To our proceeding bids me tell you this;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.108>And reason to my love is liable.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.109>How foolish do your fears seem now, Calpurnia!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.110>I am ashamed I did yield to them.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.111>Give me my robe, for I will go.</p>
<p><i>Enter PUBLIUS, BRUTUS, LIGARIUS, METELLUS, CASCA, TREBONIUS, and CINNA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.112>And look where Publius is come to fetch me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>PUBLIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.113>Good morrow, Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.114>Welcome, Publius.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.115>What, Brutus, are you stirr'd so early too?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.116>Good morrow, Casca. Caius Ligarius,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.117>Caesar was ne'er so much your enemy</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.118>As that same ague which hath made you lean.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.119>What is 't o'clock?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.120>Caesar, 'tis strucken eight.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.121>I thank you for your pains and courtesy.</p>
<p><i>Enter ANTONY</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.122>See! Antony, that revels long o' nights,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.123>Is notwithstanding up. Good morrow, Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.124>So to most noble Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.125>Bid them prepare within:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.126>I am to blame to be thus waited for.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.127>Now, Cinna: now, Metellus: what, Trebonius!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.128>I have an hour's talk in store for you;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.129>Remember that you call on me to-day:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.130>Be near me, that I may remember you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>TREBONIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.131>Caesar, I will:</p>
<p><i>Aside</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.132>and so near will I be,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.133>That your best friends shall wish I had been further.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.134>Good friends, go in, and taste some wine with me;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.135>And we, like friends, will straightway go together.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.136>[Aside]  That every like is not the same, O Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.137>The heart of Brutus yearns to think upon!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. A street near the Capitol.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter ARTEMIDORUS, reading a paper</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>ARTEMIDORUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.1>'Caesar, beware of Brutus; take heed of Cassius;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.2>come not near Casca; have an eye to Cinna, trust not</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.3>Trebonius: mark well Metellus Cimber: Decius Brutus</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.4>loves thee not: thou hast wronged Caius Ligarius.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.5>There is but one mind in all these men, and it is</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.6>bent against Caesar. If thou beest not immortal,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.7>look about you: security gives way to conspiracy.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.8>The mighty gods defend thee! Thy lover,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.9>'ARTEMIDORUS.'</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.10>Here will I stand till Caesar pass along,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.11>And as a suitor will I give him this.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.12>My heart laments that virtue cannot live</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.13>Out of the teeth of emulation.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.14>If thou read this, O Caesar, thou mayst live;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.15>If not, the Fates with traitors do contrive.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE IV. Another part of the same street, before the house of BRUTUS.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter PORTIA and LUCIUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.1>I prithee, boy, run to the senate-house;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.2>Stay not to answer me, but get thee gone:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.3>Why dost thou stay?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.4>To know my errand, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.5>I would have had thee there, and here again,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.6>Ere I can tell thee what thou shouldst do there.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.7>O constancy, be strong upon my side,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.8>Set a huge mountain 'tween my heart and tongue!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.9>I have a man's mind, but a woman's might.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.10>How hard it is for women to keep counsel!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.11>Art thou here yet?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.12>                  Madam, what should I do?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.13>Run to the Capitol, and nothing else?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.14>And so return to you, and nothing else?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.15>Yes, bring me word, boy, if thy lord look well,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.16>For he went sickly forth: and take good note</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.17>What Caesar doth, what suitors press to him.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.18>Hark, boy! what noise is that?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.19>I hear none, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.20>Prithee, listen well;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.21>I heard a bustling rumour, like a fray,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.22>And the wind brings it from the Capitol.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.23>Sooth, madam, I hear nothing.</p>
<p><i>Enter the Soothsayer</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.24>Come hither, fellow: which way hast thou been?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Soothsayer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.25>At mine own house, good lady.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.26>What is't o'clock?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Soothsayer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.27>                  About the ninth hour, lady.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.28>Is Caesar yet gone to the Capitol?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>Soothsayer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.29>Madam, not yet: I go to take my stand,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.30>To see him pass on to the Capitol.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.31>Thou hast some suit to Caesar, hast thou not?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Soothsayer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.32>That I have, lady: if it will please Caesar</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.33>To be so good to Caesar as to hear me,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.34>I shall beseech him to befriend himself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.35>Why, know'st thou any harm's intended towards him?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>Soothsayer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.36>None that I know will be, much that I fear may chance.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.37>Good morrow to you. Here the street is narrow:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.38>The throng that follows Caesar at the heels,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.39>Of senators, of praetors, common suitors,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.40>Will crowd a feeble man almost to death:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.41>I'll get me to a place more void, and there</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.42>Speak to great Caesar as he comes along.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>PORTIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.43>I must go in. Ay me, how weak a thing</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.44>The heart of woman is! O Brutus,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.45>The heavens speed thee in thine enterprise!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.46>Sure, the boy heard me: Brutus hath a suit</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.47>That Caesar will not grant. O, I grow faint.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.48>Run, Lucius, and commend me to my lord;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.49>Say I am merry: come to me again,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.50>And bring me word what he doth say to thee.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt severally</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT III</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Rome. Before the Capitol; the Senate sitting above.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>A crowd of people; among them ARTEMIDORUS and the  Soothsayer. Flourish. Enter CAESAR, BRUTUS,  CASSIUS, CASCA, DECIUS BRUTUS, METELLUS CIMBER,  TREBONIUS, CINNA, ANTONY, LEPIDUS, POPILIUS, PUBLIUS, and others</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.1>[To the Soothsayer]  The ides of March are come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Soothsayer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.2>Ay, Caesar; but not gone.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>ARTEMIDORUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.3>Hail, Caesar! read this schedule.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>DECIUS BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.4>Trebonius doth desire you to o'erread,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.5>At your best leisure, this his humble suit.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>ARTEMIDORUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.6>O Caesar, read mine first; for mine's a suit</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.7>That touches Caesar nearer: read it, great Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.8>What touches us ourself shall be last served.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>ARTEMIDORUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.9>Delay not, Caesar; read it instantly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.10>What, is the fellow mad?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>PUBLIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.11>Sirrah, give place.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.12>What, urge you your petitions in the street?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.13>Come to the Capitol.</p>
<p><i>CAESAR goes up to the Senate-House, the rest following</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>POPILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.14>I wish your enterprise to-day may thrive.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.15>What enterprise, Popilius?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>POPILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.16>Fare you well.</p>
<p><i>Advances to CAESAR</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.17>What said Popilius Lena?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.18>He wish'd to-day our enterprise might thrive.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.19>I fear our purpose is discovered.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.20>Look, how he makes to Caesar; mark him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.21>Casca, be sudden, for we fear prevention.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.22>Brutus, what shall be done? If this be known,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.23>Cassius or Caesar never shall turn back,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.24>For I will slay myself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.25>Cassius, be constant:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.26>Popilius Lena speaks not of our purposes;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.27>For, look, he smiles, and Caesar doth not change.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.28>Trebonius knows his time; for, look you, Brutus.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.29>He draws Mark Antony out of the way.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt ANTONY and TREBONIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>DECIUS BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.30>Where is Metellus Cimber? Let him go,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.31>And presently prefer his suit to Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.32>He is address'd: press near and second him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>CINNA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.33>Casca, you are the first that rears your hand.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.34>Are we all ready? What is now amiss</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.35>That Caesar and his senate must redress?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>METELLUS CIMBER</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.36>Most high, most mighty, and most puissant Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.37>Metellus Cimber throws before thy seat</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.38>An humble heart,--</p>
<p><i>Kneeling</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.39>                  I must prevent thee, Cimber.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.40>These couchings and these lowly courtesies</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.41>Might fire the blood of ordinary men,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.42>And turn pre-ordinance and first decree</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.43>Into the law of children. Be not fond,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.44>To think that Caesar bears such rebel blood</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.45>That will be thaw'd from the true quality</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.46>With that which melteth fools; I mean, sweet words,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.47>Low-crooked court'sies and base spaniel-fawning.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.48>Thy brother by decree is banished:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.49>If thou dost bend and pray and fawn for him,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.50>I spurn thee like a cur out of my way.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.51>Know, Caesar doth not wrong, nor without cause</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.52>Will he be satisfied.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>METELLUS CIMBER</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.53>Is there no voice more worthy than my own</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.54>To sound more sweetly in great Caesar's ear</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.55>For the repealing of my banish'd brother?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.56>I kiss thy hand, but not in flattery, Caesar;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.57>Desiring thee that Publius Cimber may</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.58>Have an immediate freedom of repeal.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.59>What, Brutus!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.60>                  Pardon, Caesar; Caesar, pardon:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.61>As low as to thy foot doth Cassius fall,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.62>To beg enfranchisement for Publius Cimber.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.63>I could be well moved, if I were as you:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.64>If I could pray to move, prayers would move me:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.65>But I am constant as the northern star,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.66>Of whose true-fix'd and resting quality</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.67>There is no fellow in the firmament.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.68>The skies are painted with unnumber'd sparks,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.69>They are all fire and every one doth shine,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.70>But there's but one in all doth hold his place:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.71>So in the world; 'tis furnish'd well with men,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.72>And men are flesh and blood, and apprehensive;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.73>Yet in the number I do know but one</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.74>That unassailable holds on his rank,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.75>Unshaked of motion: and that I am he,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.76>Let me a little show it, even in this;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.77>That I was constant Cimber should be banish'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.78>And constant do remain to keep him so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>CINNA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.79>O Caesar,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.80>          Hence! wilt thou lift up Olympus?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>DECIUS BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.81>Great Caesar,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.82>                  Doth not Brutus bootless kneel?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>CASCA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.83>Speak, hands for me!</p>
<p><i>CASCA first, then the other Conspirators and BRUTUS stab CAESAR</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.84>Et tu, Brute! Then fall, Caesar.</p>
<p><i>Dies</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>CINNA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.85>Liberty! Freedom! Tyranny is dead!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.86>Run hence, proclaim, cry it about the streets.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.87>Some to the common pulpits, and cry out</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.88>'Liberty, freedom, and enfranchisement!'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.89>People and senators, be not affrighted;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.90>Fly not; stand stiff: ambition's debt is paid.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>CASCA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.91>Go to the pulpit, Brutus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>DECIUS BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.92>And Cassius too.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.93>Where's Publius?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>CINNA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.94>Here, quite confounded with this mutiny.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>METELLUS CIMBER</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.95>Stand fast together, lest some friend of Caesar's</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.96>Should chance--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.97>Talk not of standing. Publius, good cheer;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.98>There is no harm intended to your person,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.99>Nor to no Roman else: so tell them, Publius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.100>And leave us, Publius; lest that the people,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.101>Rushing on us, should do your age some mischief.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.102>Do so: and let no man abide this deed,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.103>But we the doers.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter TREBONIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.104>                  Where is Antony?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>TREBONIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.105>Fled to his house amazed:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.106>Men, wives and children stare, cry out and run</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.107>As it were doomsday.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.108>Fates, we will know your pleasures:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.109>That we shall die, we know; 'tis but the time</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.110>And drawing days out, that men stand upon.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.111>Why, he that cuts off twenty years of life</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.112>Cuts off so many years of fearing death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.113>Grant that, and then is death a benefit:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.114>So are we Caesar's friends, that have abridged</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.115>His time of fearing death. Stoop, Romans, stoop,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.116>And let us bathe our hands in Caesar's blood</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.117>Up to the elbows, and besmear our swords:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.118>Then walk we forth, even to the market-place,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.119>And, waving our red weapons o'er our heads,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.120>Let's all cry 'Peace, freedom and liberty!'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.121>Stoop, then, and wash. How many ages hence</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.122>Shall this our lofty scene be acted over</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.123>In states unborn and accents yet unknown!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.124>How many times shall Caesar bleed in sport,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.125>That now on Pompey's basis lies along</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.126>No worthier than the dust!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.127>So oft as that shall be,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.128>So often shall the knot of us be call'd</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.129>The men that gave their country liberty.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>DECIUS BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.130>What, shall we forth?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.131>Ay, every man away:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.132>Brutus shall lead; and we will grace his heels</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.133>With the most boldest and best hearts of Rome.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Servant</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.134>Soft! who comes here? A friend of Antony's.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.135>Thus, Brutus, did my master bid me kneel:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.136>Thus did Mark Antony bid me fall down;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.137>And, being prostrate, thus he bade me say:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.138>Brutus is noble, wise, valiant, and honest;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.139>Caesar was mighty, bold, royal, and loving:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.140>Say I love Brutus, and I honour him;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.141>Say I fear'd Caesar, honour'd him and loved him.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.142>If Brutus will vouchsafe that Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.143>May safely come to him, and be resolved</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.144>How Caesar hath deserved to lie in death,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.145>Mark Antony shall not love Caesar dead</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.146>So well as Brutus living; but will follow</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.147>The fortunes and affairs of noble Brutus</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.148>Thorough the hazards of this untrod state</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.149>With all true faith. So says my master Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.150>Thy master is a wise and valiant Roman;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.151>I never thought him worse.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.152>Tell him, so please him come unto this place,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.153>He shall be satisfied; and, by my honour,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.154>Depart untouch'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.155>                  I'll fetch him presently.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.156>I know that we shall have him well to friend.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.157>I wish we may: but yet have I a mind</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.158>That fears him much; and my misgiving still</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.159>Falls shrewdly to the purpose.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.160>But here comes Antony.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter ANTONY</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.161>Welcome, Mark Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.162>O mighty Caesar! dost thou lie so low?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.163>Are all thy conquests, glories, triumphs, spoils,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.164>Shrunk to this little measure? Fare thee well.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.165>I know not, gentlemen, what you intend,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.166>Who else must be let blood, who else is rank:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.167>If I myself, there is no hour so fit</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.168>As Caesar's death hour, nor no instrument</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.169>Of half that worth as those your swords, made rich</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.170>With the most noble blood of all this world.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.171>I do beseech ye, if you bear me hard,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.172>Now, whilst your purpled hands do reek and smoke,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.173>Fulfil your pleasure. Live a thousand years,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.174>I shall not find myself so apt to die:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.175>No place will please me so, no mean of death,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.176>As here by Caesar, and by you cut off,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.177>The choice and master spirits of this age.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.178>O Antony, beg not your death of us.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.179>Though now we must appear bloody and cruel,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.180>As, by our hands and this our present act,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.181>You see we do, yet see you but our hands</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.182>And this the bleeding business they have done:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.183>Our hearts you see not; they are pitiful;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.184>And pity to the general wrong of Rome--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.185>As fire drives out fire, so pity pity--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.186>Hath done this deed on Caesar. For your part,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.187>To you our swords have leaden points, Mark Antony:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.188>Our arms, in strength of malice, and our hearts</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.189>Of brothers' temper, do receive you in</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.190>With all kind love, good thoughts, and reverence.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.191>Your voice shall be as strong as any man's</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.192>In the disposing of new dignities.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.193>Only be patient till we have appeased</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.194>The multitude, beside themselves with fear,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.195>And then we will deliver you the cause,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.196>Why I, that did love Caesar when I struck him,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.197>Have thus proceeded.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.198>I doubt not of your wisdom.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.199>Let each man render me his bloody hand:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.200>First, Marcus Brutus, will I shake with you;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.201>Next, Caius Cassius, do I take your hand;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.202>Now, Decius Brutus, yours: now yours, Metellus;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.203>Yours, Cinna; and, my valiant Casca, yours;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.204>Though last, not last in love, yours, good Trebonius.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.205>Gentlemen all,--alas, what shall I say?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.206>My credit now stands on such slippery ground,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.207>That one of two bad ways you must conceit me,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.208>Either a coward or a flatterer.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.209>That I did love thee, Caesar, O, 'tis true:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.210>If then thy spirit look upon us now,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.211>Shall it not grieve thee dearer than thy death,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.212>To see thy thy Anthony making his peace,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.213>Shaking the bloody fingers of thy foes,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.214>Most noble! in the presence of thy corse?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.215>Had I as many eyes as thou hast wounds,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.216>Weeping as fast as they stream forth thy blood,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.217>It would become me better than to close</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.218>In terms of friendship with thine enemies.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.219>Pardon me, Julius! Here wast thou bay'd, brave hart;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.220>Here didst thou fall; and here thy hunters stand,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.221>Sign'd in thy spoil, and crimson'd in thy lethe.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.222>O world, thou wast the forest to this hart;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.223>And this, indeed, O world, the heart of thee.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.224>How like a deer, strucken by many princes,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.225>Dost thou here lie!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.226>Mark Antony,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.227>                  Pardon me, Caius Cassius:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.228>The enemies of Caesar shall say this;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.229>Then, in a friend, it is cold modesty.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.230>I blame you not for praising Caesar so;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.231>But what compact mean you to have with us?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.232>Will you be prick'd in number of our friends;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.233>Or shall we on, and not depend on you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.234>Therefore I took your hands, but was, indeed,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.235>Sway'd from the point, by looking down on Caesar.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.236>Friends am I with you all and love you all,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.237>Upon this hope, that you shall give me reasons</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.238>Why and wherein Caesar was dangerous.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.239>Or else were this a savage spectacle:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.240>Our reasons are so full of good regard</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.241>That were you, Antony, the son of Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.242>You should be satisfied.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.243>That's all I seek:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.244>And am moreover suitor that I may</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.245>Produce his body to the market-place;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.246>And in the pulpit, as becomes a friend,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.247>Speak in the order of his funeral.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.248>You shall, Mark Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.249>Brutus, a word with you.</p>
<p><i>Aside to BRUTUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.250>You know not what you do: do not consent</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.251>That Antony speak in his funeral:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.252>Know you how much the people may be moved</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.253>By that which he will utter?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.254>By your pardon;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.255>I will myself into the pulpit first,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.256>And show the reason of our Caesar's death:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.257>What Antony shall speak, I will protest</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.258>He speaks by leave and by permission,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.259>And that we are contented Caesar shall</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.260>Have all true rites and lawful ceremonies.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.261>It shall advantage more than do us wrong.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.262>I know not what may fall; I like it not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.263>Mark Antony, here, take you Caesar's body.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.264>You shall not in your funeral speech blame us,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.265>But speak all good you can devise of Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.266>And say you do't by our permission;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.267>Else shall you not have any hand at all</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.268>About his funeral: and you shall speak</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.269>In the same pulpit whereto I am going,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.270>After my speech is ended.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.271>Be it so.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.272>I do desire no more.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.273>Prepare the body then, and follow us.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt all but ANTONY</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.274>O, pardon me, thou bleeding piece of earth,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.275>That I am meek and gentle with these butchers!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.276>Thou art the ruins of the noblest man</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.277>That ever lived in the tide of times.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.278>Woe to the hand that shed this costly blood!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.279>Over thy wounds now do I prophesy,--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.280>Which, like dumb mouths, do ope their ruby lips,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.281>To beg the voice and utterance of my tongue--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.282>A curse shall light upon the limbs of men;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.283>Domestic fury and fierce civil strife</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.284>Shall cumber all the parts of Italy;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.285>Blood and destruction shall be so in use</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.286>And dreadful objects so familiar</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.287>That mothers shall but smile when they behold</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.288>Their infants quarter'd with the hands of war;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.289>All pity choked with custom of fell deeds:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.290>And Caesar's spirit, ranging for revenge,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.291>With Ate by his side come hot from hell,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.292>Shall in these confines with a monarch's voice</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.293>Cry  'Havoc,' and let slip the dogs of war;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.294>That this foul deed shall smell above the earth</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.295>With carrion men, groaning for burial.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Servant</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.296>You serve Octavius Caesar, do you not?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.297>I do, Mark Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech85><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.298>Caesar did write for him to come to Rome.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech86><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.299>He did receive his letters, and is coming;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.300>And bid me say to you by word of mouth--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.301>O Caesar!--</p>
<p><i>Seeing the body</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech87><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.302>Thy heart is big, get thee apart and weep.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.303>Passion, I see, is catching; for mine eyes,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.304>Seeing those beads of sorrow stand in thine,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.305>Began to water. Is thy master coming?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech88><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.306>He lies to-night within seven leagues of Rome.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech89><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.307>Post back with speed, and tell him what hath chanced:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.308>Here is a mourning Rome, a dangerous Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.309>No Rome of safety for Octavius yet;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.310>Hie hence, and tell him so. Yet, stay awhile;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.311>Thou shalt not back till I have borne this corse</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.312>Into the market-place: there shall I try</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.313>In my oration, how the people take</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.314>The cruel issue of these bloody men;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.315>According to the which, thou shalt discourse</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.316>To young Octavius of the state of things.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.317>Lend me your hand.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt with CAESAR's body</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. The Forum.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter BRUTUS and CASSIUS, and a throng of Citizens</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.1>We will be satisfied; let us be satisfied.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.2>Then follow me, and give me audience, friends.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.3>Cassius, go you into the other street,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.4>And part the numbers.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.5>Those that will hear me speak, let 'em stay here;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.6>Those that will follow Cassius, go with him;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.7>And public reasons shall be rendered</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.8>Of Caesar's death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.9>                  I will hear Brutus speak.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.10>I will hear Cassius; and compare their reasons,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.11>When severally we hear them rendered.</p>
<p><i>Exit CASSIUS, with some of the Citizens. BRUTUS goes into the pulpit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.12>The noble Brutus is ascended: silence!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.13>Be patient till the last.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.14>Romans, countrymen, and lovers! hear me for my</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.15>cause, and be silent, that you may hear: believe me</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.16>for mine honour, and have respect to mine honour, that</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.17>you may believe: censure me in your wisdom, and</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.18>awake your senses, that you may the better judge.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.19>If there be any in this assembly, any dear friend of</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.20>Caesar's, to him I say, that Brutus' love to Caesar</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.21>was no less than his. If then that friend demand</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.22>why Brutus rose against Caesar, this is my answer:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.23>--Not that I loved Caesar less, but that I loved</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.24>Rome more. Had you rather Caesar were living and</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.25>die all slaves, than that Caesar were dead, to live</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.26>all free men? As Caesar loved me, I weep for him;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.27>as he was fortunate, I rejoice at it; as he was</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.28>valiant, I honour him: but, as he was ambitious, I</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.29>slew him. There is tears for his love; joy for his</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.30>fortune; honour for his valour; and death for his</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.31>ambition. Who is here so base that would be a</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.32>bondman? If any, speak; for him have I offended.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.33>Who is here so rude that would not be a Roman? If</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.34>any, speak; for him have I offended. Who is here so</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.35>vile that will not love his country? If any, speak;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.36>for him have I offended. I pause for a reply.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.37>None, Brutus, none.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.38>Then none have I offended. I have done no more to</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.39>Caesar than you shall do to Brutus. The question of</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.40>his death is enrolled in the Capitol; his glory not</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.41>extenuated, wherein he was worthy, nor his offences</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.42>enforced, for which he suffered death.</p>
<p><i>Enter ANTONY and others, with CAESAR's body</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.43>Here comes his body, mourned by Mark Antony: who,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.44>though he had no hand in his death, shall receive</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.45>the benefit of his dying, a place in the</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.46>commonwealth; as which of you shall not? With this</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.47>I depart,--that, as I slew my best lover for the</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.48>good of Rome, I have the same dagger for myself,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.49>when it shall please my country to need my death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.50>Live, Brutus! live, live!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.51>Bring him with triumph home unto his house.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.52>Give him a statue with his ancestors.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.53>Let him be Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.54>                  Caesar's better parts</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.55>Shall be crown'd in Brutus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.56>We'll bring him to his house</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.57>With shouts and clamours.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.58>My countrymen,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.59>Peace, silence! Brutus speaks.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.60>Peace, ho!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.61>Good countrymen, let me depart alone,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.62>And, for my sake, stay here with Antony:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.63>Do grace to Caesar's corpse, and grace his speech</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.64>Tending to Caesar's glories; which Mark Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.65>By our permission, is allow'd to make.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.66>I do entreat you, not a man depart,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.67>Save I alone, till Antony have spoke.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.68>Stay, ho! and let us hear Mark Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.69>Let him go up into the public chair;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.70>We'll hear him. Noble Antony, go up.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.71>For Brutus' sake, I am beholding to you.</p>
<p><i>Goes into the pulpit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.72>What does he say of Brutus?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.73>He says, for Brutus' sake,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.74>He finds himself beholding to us all.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.75>'Twere best he speak no harm of Brutus here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.76>This Caesar was a tyrant.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.77>Nay, that's certain:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.78>We are blest that Rome is rid of him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.79>Peace! let us hear what Antony can say.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.80>You gentle Romans,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.81>Peace, ho! let us hear him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.82>Friends, Romans, countrymen, lend me your ears;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.83>I come to bury Caesar, not to praise him.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.84>The evil that men do lives after them;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.85>The good is oft interred with their bones;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.86>So let it be with Caesar. The noble Brutus</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.87>Hath told you Caesar was ambitious:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.88>If it were so, it was a grievous fault,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.89>And grievously hath Caesar answer'd it.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.90>Here, under leave of Brutus and the rest--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.91>For Brutus is an honourable man;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.92>So are they all, all honourable men--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.93>Come I to speak in Caesar's funeral.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.94>He was my friend, faithful and just to me:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.95>But Brutus says he was ambitious;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.96>And Brutus is an honourable man.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.97>He hath brought many captives home to Rome</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.98>Whose ransoms did the general coffers fill:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.99>Did this in Caesar seem ambitious?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.100>When that the poor have cried, Caesar hath wept:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.101>Ambition should be made of sterner stuff:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.102>Yet Brutus says he was ambitious;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.103>And Brutus is an honourable man.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.104>You all did see that on the Lupercal</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.105>I thrice presented him a kingly crown,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.106>Which he did thrice refuse: was this ambition?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.107>Yet Brutus says he was ambitious;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.108>And, sure, he is an honourable man.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.109>I speak not to disprove what Brutus spoke,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.110>But here I am to speak what I do know.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.111>You all did love him once, not without cause:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.112>What cause withholds you then, to mourn for him?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.113>O judgment! thou art fled to brutish beasts,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.114>And men have lost their reason. Bear with me;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.115>My heart is in the coffin there with Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.116>And I must pause till it come back to me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.117>Methinks there is much reason in his sayings.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.118>If thou consider rightly of the matter,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.119>Caesar has had great wrong.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.120>Has he, masters?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.121>I fear there will a worse come in his place.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.122>Mark'd ye his words? He would not take the crown;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.123>Therefore 'tis certain he was not ambitious.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.124>If it be found so, some will dear abide it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.125>Poor soul! his eyes are red as fire with weeping.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.126>There's not a nobler man in Rome than Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.127>Now mark him, he begins again to speak.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.128>But yesterday the word of Caesar might</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.129>Have stood against the world; now lies he there.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.130>And none so poor to do him reverence.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.131>O masters, if I were disposed to stir</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.132>Your hearts and minds to mutiny and rage,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.133>I should do Brutus wrong, and Cassius wrong,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.134>Who, you all know, are honourable men:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.135>I will not do them wrong; I rather choose</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.136>To wrong the dead, to wrong myself and you,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.137>Than I will wrong such honourable men.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.138>But here's a parchment with the seal of Caesar;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.139>I found it in his closet, 'tis his will:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.140>Let but the commons hear this testament--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.141>Which, pardon me, I do not mean to read--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.142>And they would go and kiss dead Caesar's wounds</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.143>And dip their napkins in his sacred blood,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.144>Yea, beg a hair of him for memory,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.145>And, dying, mention it within their wills,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.146>Bequeathing it as a rich legacy</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.147>Unto their issue.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.148>We'll hear the will: read it, Mark Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.149>The will, the will! we will hear Caesar's will.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.150>Have patience, gentle friends, I must not read it;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.151>It is not meet you know how Caesar loved you.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.152>You are not wood, you are not stones, but men;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.153>And, being men, bearing the will of Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.154>It will inflame you, it will make you mad:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.155>'Tis good you know not that you are his heirs;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.156>For, if you should, O, what would come of it!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.157>Read the will; we'll hear it, Antony;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.158>You shall read us the will, Caesar's will.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.159>Will you be patient? will you stay awhile?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.160>I have o'ershot myself to tell you of it:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.161>I fear I wrong the honourable men</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.162>Whose daggers have stabb'd Caesar; I do fear it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.163>They were traitors: honourable men!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.164>The will! the testament!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.165>They were villains, murderers: the will! read the will.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.166>You will compel me, then, to read the will?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.167>Then make a ring about the corpse of Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.168>And let me show you him that made the will.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.169>Shall I descend? and will you give me leave?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>Several Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.170>Come down.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.171>Descend.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.172>You shall have leave.</p>
<p><i>ANTONY comes down</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.173>A ring; stand round.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.174>Stand from the hearse, stand from the body.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.175>Room for Antony, most noble Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.176>Nay, press not so upon me; stand far off.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>Several Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.177>Stand back; room; bear back.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.178>If you have tears, prepare to shed them now.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.179>You all do know this mantle: I remember</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.180>The first time ever Caesar put it on;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.181>'Twas on a summer's evening, in his tent,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.182>That day he overcame the Nervii:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.183>Look, in this place ran Cassius' dagger through:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.184>See what a rent the envious Casca made:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.185>Through this the well-beloved Brutus stabb'd;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.186>And as he pluck'd his cursed steel away,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.187>Mark how the blood of Caesar follow'd it,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.188>As rushing out of doors, to be resolved</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.189>If Brutus so unkindly knock'd, or no;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.190>For Brutus, as you know, was Caesar's angel:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.191>Judge, O you gods, how dearly Caesar loved him!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.192>This was the most unkindest cut of all;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.193>For when the noble Caesar saw him stab,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.194>Ingratitude, more strong than traitors' arms,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.195>Quite vanquish'd him: then burst his mighty heart;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.196>And, in his mantle muffling up his face,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.197>Even at the base of Pompey's statua,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.198>Which all the while ran blood, great Caesar fell.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.199>O, what a fall was there, my countrymen!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.200>Then I, and you, and all of us fell down,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.201>Whilst bloody treason flourish'd over us.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.202>O, now you weep; and, I perceive, you feel</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.203>The dint of pity: these are gracious drops.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.204>Kind souls, what, weep you when you but behold</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.205>Our Caesar's vesture wounded? Look you here,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.206>Here is himself, marr'd, as you see, with traitors.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.207>O piteous spectacle!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.208>O noble Caesar!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.209>O woful day!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.210>O traitors, villains!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.211>O most bloody sight!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.212>We will be revenged.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.213>Revenge! About! Seek! Burn! Fire! Kill! Slay!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.214>Let not a traitor live!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.215>Stay, countrymen.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.216>Peace there! hear the noble Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.217>We'll hear him, we'll follow him, we'll die with him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.218>Good friends, sweet friends, let me not stir you up</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.219>To such a sudden flood of mutiny.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.220>They that have done this deed are honourable:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.221>What private griefs they have, alas, I know not,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.222>That made them do it: they are wise and honourable,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.223>And will, no doubt, with reasons answer you.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.224>I come not, friends, to steal away your hearts:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.225>I am no orator, as Brutus is;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.226>But, as you know me all, a plain blunt man,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.227>That love my friend; and that they know full well</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.228>That gave me public leave to speak of him:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.229>For I have neither wit, nor words, nor worth,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.230>Action, nor utterance, nor the power of speech,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.231>To stir men's blood: I only speak right on;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.232>I tell you that which you yourselves do know;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.233>Show you sweet Caesar's wounds, poor poor dumb mouths,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.234>And bid them speak for me: but were I Brutus,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.235>And Brutus Antony, there were an Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.236>Would ruffle up your spirits and put a tongue</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.237>In every wound of Caesar that should move</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.238>The stones of Rome to rise and mutiny.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.239>We'll mutiny.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
