<p class="line" name=3.2.240>We'll burn the house of Brutus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.241>Away, then! come, seek the conspirators.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.242>Yet hear me, countrymen; yet hear me speak.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.243>Peace, ho! Hear Antony. Most noble Antony!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.244>Why, friends, you go to do you know not what:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.245>Wherein hath Caesar thus deserved your loves?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.246>Alas, you know not: I must tell you then:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.247>You have forgot the will I told you of.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.248>Most true. The will! Let's stay and hear the will.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.249>Here is the will, and under Caesar's seal.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.250>To every Roman citizen he gives,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.251>To every several man, seventy-five drachmas.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.252>Most noble Caesar! We'll revenge his death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.253>O royal Caesar!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.254>Hear me with patience.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.255>Peace, ho!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.256>Moreover, he hath left you all his walks,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.257>His private arbours and new-planted orchards,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.258>On this side Tiber; he hath left them you,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.259>And to your heirs for ever, common pleasures,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.260>To walk abroad, and recreate yourselves.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.261>Here was a Caesar! when comes such another?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.262>Never, never. Come, away, away!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.263>We'll burn his body in the holy place,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.264>And with the brands fire the traitors' houses.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.265>Take up the body.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.266>Go fetch fire.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.267>Pluck down benches.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech85><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.268>Pluck down forms, windows, any thing.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt Citizens with the body</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech86><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.269>Now let it work. Mischief, thou art afoot,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.270>Take thou what course thou wilt!</p>
<p><i>Enter a Servant</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.271>How now, fellow!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech87><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.272>Sir, Octavius is already come to Rome.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech88><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.273>Where is he?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech89><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.274>He and Lepidus are at Caesar's house.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech90><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.275>And thither will I straight to visit him:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.276>He comes upon a wish. Fortune is merry,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.277>And in this mood will give us any thing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech91><b>Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.278>I heard him say, Brutus and Cassius</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.279>Are rid like madmen through the gates of Rome.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech92><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.280>Belike they had some notice of the people,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.281>How I had moved them. Bring me to Octavius.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. A street.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CINNA the poet</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CINNA THE POET</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.1>I dreamt to-night that I did feast with Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.2>And things unlucky charge my fantasy:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.3>I have no will to wander forth of doors,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.4>Yet something leads me forth.</p>
<p><i>Enter Citizens</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.5>What is your name?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.6>Whither are you going?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.7>Where do you dwell?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.8>Are you a married man or a bachelor?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.9>Answer every man directly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.10>Ay, and briefly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.11>Ay, and wisely.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.12>Ay, and truly, you were best.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>CINNA THE POET</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.13>What is my name? Whither am I going? Where do I</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.14>dwell? Am I a married man or a bachelor? Then, to</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.15>answer every man directly and briefly, wisely and</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.16>truly: wisely I say, I am a bachelor.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.17>That's as much as to say, they are fools that marry:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.18>you'll bear me a bang for that, I fear. Proceed; directly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>CINNA THE POET</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.19>Directly, I am going to Caesar's funeral.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.20>As a friend or an enemy?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>CINNA THE POET</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.21>As a friend.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.22>That matter is answered directly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.23>For your dwelling,--briefly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CINNA THE POET</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.24>Briefly, I dwell by the Capitol.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.25>Your name, sir, truly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>CINNA THE POET</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.26>Truly, my name is Cinna.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.27>Tear him to pieces; he's a conspirator.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>CINNA THE POET</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.28>I am Cinna the poet, I am Cinna the poet.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.29>Tear him for his bad verses, tear him for his bad verses.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CINNA THE POET</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.30>I am not Cinna the conspirator.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.31>It is no matter, his name's Cinna; pluck but his</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.32>name out of his heart, and turn him going.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.33>Tear him, tear him! Come, brands ho! fire-brands:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.34>to Brutus', to Cassius'; burn all: some to Decius'</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.35>house, and some to Casca's; some to Ligarius': away, go!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT IV</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. A house in Rome.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>ANTONY, OCTAVIUS, and LEPIDUS, seated at a table</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.1>These many, then, shall die; their names are prick'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.2>Your brother too must die; consent you, Lepidus?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.3>I do consent--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.4>                  Prick him down, Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.5>Upon condition Publius shall not live,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.6>Who is your sister's son, Mark Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.7>He shall not live; look, with a spot I damn him.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.8>But, Lepidus, go you to Caesar's house;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.9>Fetch the will hither, and we shall determine</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.10>How to cut off some charge in legacies.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.11>What, shall I find you here?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.12>Or here, or at the Capitol.</p>
<p><i>Exit LEPIDUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.13>This is a slight unmeritable man,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.14>Meet to be sent on errands: is it fit,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.15>The three-fold world divided, he should stand</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.16>One of the three to share it?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.17>So you thought him;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.18>And took his voice who should be prick'd to die,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.19>In our black sentence and proscription.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.20>Octavius, I have seen more days than you:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.21>And though we lay these honours on this man,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.22>To ease ourselves of divers slanderous loads,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.23>He shall but bear them as the ass bears gold,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.24>To groan and sweat under the business,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.25>Either led or driven, as we point the way;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.26>And having brought our treasure where we will,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.27>Then take we down his load, and turn him off,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.28>Like to the empty ass, to shake his ears,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.29>And graze in commons.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.30>You may do your will;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.31>But he's a tried and valiant soldier.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.32>So is my horse, Octavius; and for that</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.33>I do appoint him store of provender:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.34>It is a creature that I teach to fight,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.35>To wind, to stop, to run directly on,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.36>His corporal motion govern'd by my spirit.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.37>And, in some taste, is Lepidus but so;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.38>He must be taught and train'd and bid go forth;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.39>A barren-spirited fellow; one that feeds</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.40>On abjects, orts and imitations,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.41>Which, out of use and staled by other men,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.42>Begin his fashion: do not talk of him,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.43>But as a property. And now, Octavius,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.44>Listen great things:--Brutus and Cassius</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.45>Are levying powers: we must straight make head:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.46>Therefore let our alliance be combined,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.47>Our best friends made, our means stretch'd</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.48>And let us presently go sit in council,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.49>How covert matters may be best disclosed,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.50>And open perils surest answered.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.51>Let us do so: for we are at the stake,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.52>And bay'd about with many enemies;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.53>And some that smile have in their hearts, I fear,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.54>Millions of mischiefs.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. Camp near Sardis. Before BRUTUS's tent.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Drum. Enter BRUTUS, LUCILIUS, LUCIUS, and Soldiers; TITINIUS and PINDARUS meeting them</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.1>Stand, ho!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>LUCILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.2>Give the word, ho! and stand.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.3>What now, Lucilius! is Cassius near?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>LUCILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.4>He is at hand; and Pindarus is come</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.5>To do you salutation from his master.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.6>He greets me well. Your master, Pindarus,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.7>In his own change, or by ill officers,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.8>Hath given me some worthy cause to wish</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.9>Things done, undone: but, if he be at hand,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.10>I shall be satisfied.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>PINDARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.11>I do not doubt</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.12>But that my noble master will appear</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.13>Such as he is, full of regard and honour.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.14>He is not doubted. A word, Lucilius;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.15>How he received you, let me be resolved.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>LUCILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.16>With courtesy and with respect enough;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.17>But not with such familiar instances,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.18>Nor with such free and friendly conference,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.19>As he hath used of old.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.20>Thou hast described</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.21>A hot friend cooling: ever note, Lucilius,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.22>When love begins to sicken and decay,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.23>It useth an enforced ceremony.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.24>There are no tricks in plain and simple faith;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.25>But hollow men, like horses hot at hand,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.26>Make gallant show and promise of their mettle;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.27>But when they should endure the bloody spur,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.28>They fall their crests, and, like deceitful jades,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.29>Sink in the trial. Comes his army on?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>LUCILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.30>They mean this night in Sardis to be quarter'd;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.31>The greater part, the horse in general,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.32>Are come with Cassius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.33>Hark! he is arrived.</p>
<p><i>Low march within</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.34>March gently on to meet him.</p>
<p><i>Enter CASSIUS and his powers</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.35>Stand, ho!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.36>Stand, ho! Speak the word along.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.37>Stand!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.38>Stand!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.39>Stand!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.40>Most noble brother, you have done me wrong.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.41>Judge me, you gods! wrong I mine enemies?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.42>And, if not so, how should I wrong a brother?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.43>Brutus, this sober form of yours hides wrongs;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.44>And when you do them--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.45>Cassius, be content.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.46>Speak your griefs softly: I do know you well.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.47>Before the eyes of both our armies here,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.48>Which should perceive nothing but love from us,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.49>Let us not wrangle: bid them move away;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.50>Then in my tent, Cassius, enlarge your griefs,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.51>And I will give you audience.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.52>Pindarus,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.53>Bid our commanders lead their charges off</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.54>A little from this ground.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.55>Lucilius, do you the like; and let no man</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.56>Come to our tent till we have done our conference.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.57>Let Lucius and Titinius guard our door.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. Brutus's tent.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter BRUTUS and CASSIUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.1>That you have wrong'd me doth appear in this:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.2>You have condemn'd and noted Lucius Pella</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.3>For taking bribes here of the Sardians;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.4>Wherein my letters, praying on his side,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.5>Because I knew the man, were slighted off.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.6>You wronged yourself to write in such a case.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.7>In such a time as this it is not meet</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.8>That every nice offence should bear his comment.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.9>Let me tell you, Cassius, you yourself</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.10>Are much condemn'd to have an itching palm;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.11>To sell and mart your offices for gold</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.12>To undeservers.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.13>                  I an itching palm!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.14>You know that you are Brutus that speak this,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.15>Or, by the gods, this speech were else your last.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.16>The name of Cassius honours this corruption,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.17>And chastisement doth therefore hide his head.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.18>Chastisement!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.19>Remember March, the ides of March remember:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.20>Did not great Julius bleed for justice' sake?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.21>What villain touch'd his body, that did stab,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.22>And not for justice? What, shall one of us</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.23>That struck the foremost man of all this world</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.24>But for supporting robbers, shall we now</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.25>Contaminate our fingers with base bribes,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.26>And sell the mighty space of our large honours</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.27>For so much trash as may be grasped thus?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.28>I had rather be a dog, and bay the moon,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.29>Than such a Roman.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.30>                  Brutus, bay not me;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.31>I'll not endure it: you forget yourself,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.32>To hedge me in; I am a soldier, I,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.33>Older in practise, abler than yourself</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.34>To make conditions.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.35>Go to; you are not, Cassius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.36>I am.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.37>I say you are not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.38>Urge me no more, I shall forget myself;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.39>Have mind upon your health, tempt me no further.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.40>Away, slight man!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.41>Is't possible?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.42>                  Hear me, for I will speak.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.43>Must I give way and room to your rash choler?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.44>Shall I be frighted when a madman stares?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.45>O ye gods, ye gods! must I endure all this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.46>All this! ay, more: fret till your proud heart break;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.47>Go show your slaves how choleric you are,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.48>And make your bondmen tremble. Must I budge?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.49>Must I observe you? must I stand and crouch</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.50>Under your testy humour? By the gods</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.51>You shall digest the venom of your spleen,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.52>Though it do split you; for, from this day forth,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.53>I'll use you for my mirth, yea, for my laughter,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.54>When you are waspish.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.55>Is it come to this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.56>You say you are a better soldier:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.57>Let it appear so; make your vaunting true,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.58>And it shall please me well: for mine own part,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.59>I shall be glad to learn of noble men.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.60>You wrong me every way; you wrong me, Brutus;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.61>I said, an elder soldier, not a better:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.62>Did I say 'better'?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.63>If you did, I care not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.64>When Caesar lived, he durst not thus have moved me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.65>Peace, peace! you durst not so have tempted him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.66>I durst not!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.67>No.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.68>What, durst not tempt him!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.69>For your life you durst not!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.70>Do not presume too much upon my love;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.71>I may do that I shall be sorry for.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.72>You have done that you should be sorry for.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.73>There is no terror, Cassius, in your threats,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.74>For I am arm'd so strong in honesty</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.75>That they pass by me as the idle wind,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.76>Which I respect not. I did send to you</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.77>For certain sums of gold, which you denied me:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.78>For I can raise no money by vile means:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.79>By heaven, I had rather coin my heart,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.80>And drop my blood for drachmas, than to wring</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.81>From the hard hands of peasants their vile trash</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.82>By any indirection: I did send</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.83>To you for gold to pay my legions,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.84>Which you denied me: was that done like Cassius?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.85>Should I have answer'd Caius Cassius so?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.86>When Marcus Brutus grows so covetous,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.87>To lock such rascal counters from his friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.88>Be ready, gods, with all your thunderbolts;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.89>Dash him to pieces!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.90>I denied you not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.91>You did.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.92>I did not: he was but a fool that brought</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.93>My answer back. Brutus hath rived my heart:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.94>A friend should bear his friend's infirmities,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.95>But Brutus makes mine greater than they are.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.96>I do not, till you practise them on me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.97>You love me not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.98>                  I do not like your faults.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.99>A friendly eye could never see such faults.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.100>A flatterer's would not, though they do appear</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.101>As huge as high Olympus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.102>Come, Antony, and young Octavius, come,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.103>Revenge yourselves alone on Cassius,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.104>For Cassius is aweary of the world;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.105>Hated by one he loves; braved by his brother;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.106>Cheque'd like a bondman; all his faults observed,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.107>Set in a note-book, learn'd, and conn'd by rote,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.108>To cast into my teeth. O, I could weep</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.109>My spirit from mine eyes! There is my dagger,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.110>And here my naked breast; within, a heart</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.111>Dearer than Plutus' mine, richer than gold:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.112>If that thou be'st a Roman, take it forth;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.113>I, that denied thee gold, will give my heart:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.114>Strike, as thou didst at Caesar; for, I know,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.115>When thou didst hate him worst, thou lovedst him better</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.116>Than ever thou lovedst Cassius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.117>Sheathe your dagger:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.118>Be angry when you will, it shall have scope;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.119>Do what you will, dishonour shall be humour.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.120>O Cassius, you are yoked with a lamb</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.121>That carries anger as the flint bears fire;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.122>Who, much enforced, shows a hasty spark,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.123>And straight is cold again.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.124>Hath Cassius lived</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.125>To be but mirth and laughter to his Brutus,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.126>When grief, and blood ill-temper'd, vexeth him?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.127>When I spoke that, I was ill-temper'd too.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.128>Do you confess so much? Give me your hand.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.129>And my heart too.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.130>                  O Brutus!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.131>What's the matter?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.132>Have not you love enough to bear with me,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.133>When that rash humour which my mother gave me</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.134>Makes me forgetful?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.135>Yes, Cassius; and, from henceforth,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.136>When you are over-earnest with your Brutus,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.137>He'll think your mother chides, and leave you so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>Poet</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.138>[Within]  Let me go in to see the generals;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.139>There is some grudge between 'em, 'tis not meet</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.140>They be alone.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>LUCILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.141>[Within]  You shall not come to them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>Poet</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.142>[Within]  Nothing but death shall stay me.</p>
<p><i>Enter Poet, followed by LUCILIUS, TITINIUS, and LUCIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.143>How now! what's the matter?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>Poet</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.144>For shame, you generals! what do you mean?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.145>Love, and be friends, as two such men should be;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.146>For I have seen more years, I'm sure, than ye.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.147>Ha, ha! how vilely doth this cynic rhyme!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.148>Get you hence, sirrah; saucy fellow, hence!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.149>Bear with him, Brutus; 'tis his fashion.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.150>I'll know his humour, when he knows his time:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.151>What should the wars do with these jigging fools?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.152>Companion, hence!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.153>                  Away, away, be gone.</p>
<p><i>Exit Poet</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.154>Lucilius and Titinius, bid the commanders</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.155>Prepare to lodge their companies to-night.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.156>And come yourselves, and bring Messala with you</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.157>Immediately to us.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt LUCILIUS and TITINIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.158>Lucius, a bowl of wine!</p>
<p><i>Exit LUCIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.159>I did not think you could have been so angry.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.160>O Cassius, I am sick of many griefs.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.161>Of your philosophy you make no use,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.162>If you give place to accidental evils.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.163>No man bears sorrow better. Portia is dead.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.164>Ha! Portia!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.165>She is dead.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.166>How 'scaped I killing when I cross'd you so?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.167>O insupportable and touching loss!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.168>Upon what sickness?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.169>Impatient of my absence,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.170>And grief that young Octavius with Mark Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.171>Have made themselves so strong:--for with her death</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.172>That tidings came;--with this she fell distract,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.173>And, her attendants absent, swallow'd fire.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.174>And died so?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.175>                  Even so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.176>O ye immortal gods!</p>
<p><i>Re-enter LUCIUS, with wine and taper</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.177>Speak no more of her. Give me a bowl of wine.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.178>In this I bury all unkindness, Cassius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.179>My heart is thirsty for that noble pledge.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.180>Fill, Lucius, till the wine o'erswell the cup;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.181>I cannot drink too much of Brutus' love.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.182>Come in, Titinius!</p>
<p><i>Exit LUCIUS</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter TITINIUS, with MESSALA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.183>Welcome, good Messala.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.184>Now sit we close about this taper here,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.185>And call in question our necessities.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.186>Portia, art thou gone?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.187>No more, I pray you.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.188>Messala, I have here received letters,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.189>That young Octavius and Mark Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.190>Come down upon us with a mighty power,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.191>Bending their expedition toward Philippi.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.192>Myself have letters of the selfsame tenor.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.193>With what addition?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.194>That by proscription and bills of outlawry,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.195>Octavius, Antony, and Lepidus,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.196>Have put to death an hundred senators.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.197>Therein our letters do not well agree;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.198>Mine speak of seventy senators that died</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.199>By their proscriptions, Cicero being one.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.200>Cicero one!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.201>          Cicero is dead,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.202>And by that order of proscription.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.203>Had you your letters from your wife, my lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.204>No, Messala.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech85><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.205>Nor nothing in your letters writ of her?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech86><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.206>Nothing, Messala.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech87><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.207>                  That, methinks, is strange.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech88><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.208>Why ask you? hear you aught of her in yours?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech89><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.209>No, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech90><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.210>Now, as you are a Roman, tell me true.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech91><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.211>Then like a Roman bear the truth I tell:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.212>For certain she is dead, and by strange manner.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech92><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.213>Why, farewell, Portia. We must die, Messala:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.214>With meditating that she must die once,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.215>I have the patience to endure it now.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech93><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.216>Even so great men great losses should endure.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech94><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.217>I have as much of this in art as you,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.218>But yet my nature could not bear it so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech95><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.219>Well, to our work alive. What do you think</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.220>Of marching to Philippi presently?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech96><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.221>I do not think it good.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech97><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.222>Your reason?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech98><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.223>This it is:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.224>'Tis better that the enemy seek us:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.225>So shall he waste his means, weary his soldiers,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.226>Doing himself offence; whilst we, lying still,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.227>Are full of rest, defense, and nimbleness.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech99><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.228>Good reasons must, of force, give place to better.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.229>The people 'twixt Philippi and this ground</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.230>Do stand but in a forced affection;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.231>For they have grudged us contribution:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.232>The enemy, marching along by them,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.233>By them shall make a fuller number up,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.234>Come on refresh'd, new-added, and encouraged;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.235>From which advantage shall we cut him off,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.236>If at Philippi we do face him there,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.237>These people at our back.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech100><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.238>Hear me, good brother.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech101><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.239>Under your pardon. You must note beside,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.240>That we have tried the utmost of our friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.241>Our legions are brim-full, our cause is ripe:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.242>The enemy increaseth every day;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.243>We, at the height, are ready to decline.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.244>There is a tide in the affairs of men,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.245>Which, taken at the flood, leads on to fortune;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.246>Omitted, all the voyage of their life</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.247>Is bound in shallows and in miseries.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.248>On such a full sea are we now afloat;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.249>And we must take the current when it serves,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.250>Or lose our ventures.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech102><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.251>Then, with your will, go on;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.252>We'll along ourselves, and meet them at Philippi.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech103><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.253>The deep of night is crept upon our talk,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.254>And nature must obey necessity;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.255>Which we will niggard with a little rest.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.256>There is no more to say?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech104><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.257>No more. Good night:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.258>Early to-morrow will we rise, and hence.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech105><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.259>Lucius!</p>
<p><i>Enter LUCIUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.260>My gown.</p>
<p><i>Exit LUCIUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.261>Farewell, good Messala:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.262>Good night, Titinius. Noble, noble Cassius,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.263>Good night, and good repose.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech106><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.264>O my dear brother!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.265>This was an ill beginning of the night:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.266>Never come such division 'tween our souls!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.267>Let it not, Brutus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech107><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.268>Every thing is well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech108><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.269>Good night, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech109><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.270>Good night, good brother.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech110><b>TITINIUS</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech111><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.271>Good night, Lord Brutus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech112><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.272>Farewell, every one.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt all but BRUTUS</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter LUCIUS, with the gown</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.273>Give me the gown. Where is thy instrument?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech113><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.274>Here in the tent.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech114><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.275>                  What, thou speak'st drowsily?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.276>Poor knave, I blame thee not; thou art o'er-watch'd.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.277>Call Claudius and some other of my men:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.278>I'll have them sleep on cushions in my tent.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech115><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.279>Varro and Claudius!</p>
<p><i>Enter VARRO and CLAUDIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech116><b>VARRO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.280>Calls my lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech117><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.281>I pray you, sirs, lie in my tent and sleep;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.282>It may be I shall raise you by and by</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.283>On business to my brother Cassius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech118><b>VARRO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.284>So please you, we will stand and watch your pleasure.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech119><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.285>I will not have it so: lie down, good sirs;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.286>It may be I shall otherwise bethink me.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.287>Look, Lucius, here's the book I sought for so;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.288>I put it in the pocket of my gown.</p>
<p><i>VARRO and CLAUDIUS lie down</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech120><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.289>I was sure your lordship did not give it me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech121><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.290>Bear with me, good boy, I am much forgetful.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.291>Canst thou hold up thy heavy eyes awhile,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.292>And touch thy instrument a strain or two?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech122><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.293>Ay, my lord, an't please you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech123><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.294>It does, my boy:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.295>I trouble thee too much, but thou art willing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech124><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.296>It is my duty, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech125><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.297>I should not urge thy duty past thy might;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.298>I know young bloods look for a time of rest.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech126><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.299>I have slept, my lord, already.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech127><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.300>It was well done; and thou shalt sleep again;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.301>I will not hold thee long: if I do live,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.302>I will be good to thee.</p>
<p><i>Music, and a song</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.303>This is a sleepy tune. O murderous slumber,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.304>Lay'st thou thy leaden mace upon my boy,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.305>That plays thee music? Gentle knave, good night;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.306>I will not do thee so much wrong to wake thee:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.307>If thou dost nod, thou break'st thy instrument;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.308>I'll take it from thee; and, good boy, good night.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.309>Let me see, let me see; is not the leaf turn'd down</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.310>Where I left reading? Here it is, I think.</p>
<p><i>Enter the Ghost of CAESAR</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.311>How ill this taper burns! Ha! who comes here?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.312>I think it is the weakness of mine eyes</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.313>That shapes this monstrous apparition.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.314>It comes upon me. Art thou any thing?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.315>Art thou some god, some angel, or some devil,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.316>That makest my blood cold and my hair to stare?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.317>Speak to me what thou art.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech128><b>GHOST</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.318>Thy evil spirit, Brutus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech129><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.319>Why comest thou?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech130><b>GHOST</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.320>To tell thee thou shalt see me at Philippi.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech131><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.321>Well; then I shall see thee again?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech132><b>GHOST</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.322>Ay, at Philippi.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech133><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.323>Why, I will see thee at Philippi, then.</p>
<p><i>Exit Ghost</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.324>Now I have taken heart thou vanishest:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.325>Ill spirit, I would hold more talk with thee.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.326>Boy, Lucius! Varro! Claudius! Sirs, awake! Claudius!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech134><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.327>The strings, my lord, are false.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech135><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.328>He thinks he still is at his instrument.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.329>Lucius, awake!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech136><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.330>My lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech137><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.331>Didst thou dream, Lucius, that thou so criedst out?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech138><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.332>My lord, I do not know that I did cry.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech139><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.333>Yes, that thou didst: didst thou see any thing?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech140><b>LUCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.334>Nothing, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech141><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.335>Sleep again, Lucius. Sirrah Claudius!</p>
<p><i>To VARRO</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.336>Fellow thou, awake!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech142><b>VARRO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.337>My lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech143><b>CLAUDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.338>My lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech144><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.339>Why did you so cry out, sirs, in your sleep?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech145><b>VARRO</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech146><b>CLAUDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.340>Did we, my lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech147><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.341>Ay: saw you any thing?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech148><b>VARRO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.342>No, my lord, I saw nothing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech149><b>CLAUDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.343>Nor I, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech150><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.344>Go and commend me to my brother Cassius;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.345>Bid him set on his powers betimes before,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.346>And we will follow.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech151><b>VARRO</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech152><b>CLAUDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.347>It shall be done, my lord.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT V</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. The plains of Philippi.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter OCTAVIUS, ANTONY, and their army</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.1>Now, Antony, our hopes are answered:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.2>You said the enemy would not come down,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.3>But keep the hills and upper regions;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.4>It proves not so: their battles are at hand;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.5>They mean to warn us at Philippi here,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.6>Answering before we do demand of them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.7>Tut, I am in their bosoms, and I know</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.8>Wherefore they do it: they could be content</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.9>To visit other places; and come down</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.10>With fearful bravery, thinking by this face</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.11>To fasten in our thoughts that they have courage;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.12>But 'tis not so.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Messenger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.13>                  Prepare you, generals:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.14>The enemy comes on in gallant show;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.15>Their bloody sign of battle is hung out,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.16>And something to be done immediately.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.17>Octavius, lead your battle softly on,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.18>Upon the left hand of the even field.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.19>Upon the right hand I; keep thou the left.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.20>Why do you cross me in this exigent?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.21>I do not cross you; but I will do so.</p>
<p><i>March</i></p>
<p><i>Drum. Enter BRUTUS, CASSIUS, and their Army; LUCILIUS, TITINIUS, MESSALA, and others</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.22>They stand, and would have parley.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.23>Stand fast, Titinius: we must out and talk.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.24>Mark Antony, shall we give sign of battle?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.25>No, Caesar, we will answer on their charge.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.26>Make forth; the generals would have some words.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.27>Stir not until the signal.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.28>Words before blows: is it so, countrymen?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.29>Not that we love words better, as you do.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.30>Good words are better than bad strokes, Octavius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.31>In your bad strokes, Brutus, you give good words:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.32>Witness the hole you made in Caesar's heart,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.33>Crying 'Long live! hail, Caesar!'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.34>Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.35>The posture of your blows are yet unknown;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.36>But for your words, they rob the Hybla bees,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.37>And leave them honeyless.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.38>Not stingless too.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.39>O, yes, and soundless too;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.40>For you have stol'n their buzzing, Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.41>And very wisely threat before you sting.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.42>Villains, you did not so, when your vile daggers</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.43>Hack'd one another in the sides of Caesar:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.44>You show'd your teeth like apes, and fawn'd like hounds,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.45>And bow'd like bondmen, kissing Caesar's feet;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.46>Whilst damned Casca, like a cur, behind</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.47>Struck Caesar on the neck. O you flatterers!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.48>Flatterers! Now, Brutus, thank yourself:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.49>This tongue had not offended so to-day,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.50>If Cassius might have ruled.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.51>Come, come, the cause: if arguing make us sweat,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.52>The proof of it will turn to redder drops. Look;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.53>I draw a sword against conspirators;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.54>When think you that the sword goes up again?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.55>Never, till Caesar's three and thirty wounds</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.56>Be well avenged; or till another Caesar</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.57>Have added slaughter to the sword of traitors.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.58>Caesar, thou canst not die by traitors' hands,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.59>Unless thou bring'st them with thee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.60>So I hope;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.61>I was not born to die on Brutus' sword.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.62>O, if thou wert the noblest of thy strain,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.63>Young man, thou couldst not die more honourable.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.64>A peevish schoolboy, worthless of such honour,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.65>Join'd with a masker and a reveller!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.66>Old Cassius still!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.67>                  Come, Antony, away!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.68>Defiance, traitors, hurl we in your teeth:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.69>If you dare fight to-day, come to the field;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.70>If not, when you have stomachs.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt OCTAVIUS, ANTONY, and their army</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.71>Why, now, blow wind, swell billow and swim bark!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.72>The storm is up, and all is on the hazard.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.73>Ho, Lucilius! hark, a word with you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>LUCILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.74>[Standing forth]	My lord?</p>
<p><i>BRUTUS and LUCILIUS converse apart</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.75>Messala!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.76>[Standing forth]  What says my general?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.77>Messala,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.78>This is my birth-day; as this very day</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.79>Was Cassius born. Give me thy hand, Messala:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.80>Be thou my witness that against my will,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.81>As Pompey was, am I compell'd to set</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.82>Upon one battle all our liberties.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.83>You know that I held Epicurus strong</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.84>And his opinion: now I change my mind,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.85>And partly credit things that do presage.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.86>Coming from Sardis, on our former ensign</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.87>Two mighty eagles fell, and there they perch'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.88>Gorging and feeding from our soldiers' hands;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.89>Who to Philippi here consorted us:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.90>This morning are they fled away and gone;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.91>And in their steads do ravens, crows and kites,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.92>Fly o'er our heads and downward look on us,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.93>As we were sickly prey: their shadows seem</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.94>A canopy most fatal, under which</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.95>Our army lies, ready to give up the ghost.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.96>Believe not so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.97>                  I but believe it partly;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.98>For I am fresh of spirit and resolved</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.99>To meet all perils very constantly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.100>Even so, Lucilius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.101>                  Now, most noble Brutus,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.102>The gods to-day stand friendly, that we may,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.103>Lovers in peace, lead on our days to age!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.104>But since the affairs of men rest still incertain,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.105>Let's reason with the worst that may befall.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.106>If we do lose this battle, then is this</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.107>The very last time we shall speak together:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.108>What are you then determined to do?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.109>Even by the rule of that philosophy</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.110>By which I did blame Cato for the death</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.111>Which he did give himself, I know not how,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.112>But I do find it cowardly and vile,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.113>For fear of what might fall, so to prevent</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.114>The time of life: arming myself with patience</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.115>To stay the providence of some high powers</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.116>That govern us below.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.117>Then, if we lose this battle,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.118>You are contented to be led in triumph</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.119>Thorough the streets of Rome?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.120>No, Cassius, no: think not, thou noble Roman,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.121>That ever Brutus will go bound to Rome;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.122>He bears too great a mind. But this same day</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.123>Must end that work the ides of March begun;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.124>And whether we shall meet again I know not.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.125>Therefore our everlasting farewell take:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.126>For ever, and for ever, farewell, Cassius!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.127>If we do meet again, why, we shall smile;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.128>If not, why then, this parting was well made.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.129>For ever, and for ever, farewell, Brutus!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.130>If we do meet again, we'll smile indeed;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.131>If not, 'tis true this parting was well made.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.132>Why, then, lead on. O, that a man might know</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.133>The end of this day's business ere it come!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.134>But it sufficeth that the day will end,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.135>And then the end is known. Come, ho! away!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. The same. The field of battle.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Alarum. Enter BRUTUS and MESSALA</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.1>Ride, ride, Messala, ride, and give these bills</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.2>Unto the legions on the other side.</p>
<p><i>Loud alarum</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.3>Let them set on at once; for I perceive</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.4>But cold demeanor in Octavius' wing,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.5>And sudden push gives them the overthrow.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.6>Ride, ride, Messala: let them all come down.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. Another part of the field.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Alarums. Enter CASSIUS and TITINIUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.1>O, look, Titinius, look, the villains fly!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.2>Myself have to mine own turn'd enemy:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.3>This ensign here of mine was turning back;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.4>I slew the coward, and did take it from him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>TITINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.5>O Cassius, Brutus gave the word too early;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.6>Who, having some advantage on Octavius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.7>Took it too eagerly: his soldiers fell to spoil,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.8>Whilst we by Antony are all enclosed.</p>
<p><i>Enter PINDARUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>PINDARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.9>Fly further off, my lord, fly further off;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.10>Mark Antony is in your tents, my lord</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.11>Fly, therefore, noble Cassius, fly far off.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.12>This hill is far enough. Look, look, Titinius;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.13>Are those my tents where I perceive the fire?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>TITINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.14>They are, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.15>                  Titinius, if thou lovest me,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.16>Mount thou my horse, and hide thy spurs in him,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.17>Till he have brought thee up to yonder troops,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.18>And here again; that I may rest assured</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.19>Whether yond troops are friend or enemy.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>TITINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.20>I will be here again, even with a thought.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.21>Go, Pindarus, get higher on that hill;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.22>My sight was ever thick; regard Titinius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.23>And tell me what thou notest about the field.</p>
<p><i>PINDARUS ascends the hill</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.24>This day I breathed first: time is come round,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.25>And where I did begin, there shall I end;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.26>My life is run his compass. Sirrah, what news?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>PINDARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.27>[Above]  O my lord!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.28>What news?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>PINDARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.29>[Above]  Titinius is enclosed round about</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.30>With horsemen, that make to him on the spur;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.31>Yet he spurs on. Now they are almost on him.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.32>Now, Titinius! Now some light. O, he lights too.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.33>He's ta'en.</p>
<p><i>Shout</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.34>And, hark! they shout for joy.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>CASSIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.35>Come down, behold no more.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.36>O, coward that I am, to live so long,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.37>To see my best friend ta'en before my face!</p>
<p><i>PINDARUS descends</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.38>Come hither, sirrah:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.39>In Parthia did I take thee prisoner;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.40>And then I swore thee, saving of thy life,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.41>That whatsoever I did bid thee do,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.42>Thou shouldst attempt it. Come now, keep thine oath;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.43>Now be a freeman: and with this good sword,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.44>That ran through Caesar's bowels, search this bosom.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.45>Stand not to answer: here, take thou the hilts;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.46>And, when my face is cover'd, as 'tis now,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.47>Guide thou the sword.</p>
<p><i>PINDARUS stabs him</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.48>Caesar, thou art revenged,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.49>Even with the sword that kill'd thee.</p>
<p><i>Dies</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>PINDARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.50>So, I am free; yet would not so have been,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.51>Durst I have done my will. O Cassius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.52>Far from this country Pindarus shall run,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.53>Where never Roman shall take note of him.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter TITINIUS with MESSALA</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.54>It is but change, Titinius; for Octavius</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.55>Is overthrown by noble Brutus' power,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.56>As Cassius' legions are by Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>TITINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.57>These tidings will well comfort Cassius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.58>Where did you leave him?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>TITINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.59>All disconsolate,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.60>With Pindarus his bondman, on this hill.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.61>Is not that he t hat lies upon the ground?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>TITINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.62>He lies not like the living. O my heart!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.63>Is not that he?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>TITINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.64>                  No, this was he, Messala,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.65>But Cassius is no more. O setting sun,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.66>As in thy red rays thou dost sink to-night,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.67>So in his red blood Cassius' day is set;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.68>The sun of Rome is set! Our day is gone;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.69>Clouds, dews, and dangers come; our deeds are done!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.70>Mistrust of my success hath done this deed.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.71>Mistrust of good success hath done this deed.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.72>O hateful error, melancholy's child,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.73>Why dost thou show to the apt thoughts of men</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.74>The things that are not? O error, soon conceived,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.75>Thou never comest unto a happy birth,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.76>But kill'st the mother that engender'd thee!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>TITINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.77>What, Pindarus! where art thou, Pindarus?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.78>Seek him, Titinius, whilst I go to meet</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.79>The noble Brutus, thrusting this report</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.80>Into his ears; I may say, thrusting it;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.81>For piercing steel and darts envenomed</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.82>Shall be as welcome to the ears of Brutus</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.83>As tidings of this sight.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>TITINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.84>Hie you, Messala,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.85>And I will seek for Pindarus the while.</p>
<p><i>Exit MESSALA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.86>Why didst thou send me forth, brave Cassius?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.87>Did I not meet thy friends? and did not they</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.88>Put on my brows this wreath of victory,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.89>And bid me give it thee? Didst thou not hear their shouts?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.90>Alas, thou hast misconstrued every thing!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.91>But, hold thee, take this garland on thy brow;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.92>Thy Brutus bid me give it thee, and I</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.93>Will do his bidding. Brutus, come apace,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.94>And see how I regarded Caius Cassius.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.95>By your leave, gods:--this is a Roman's part</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.96>Come, Cassius' sword, and find Titinius' heart.</p>
<p><i>Kills himself</i></p>
<p><i>Alarum. Re-enter MESSALA, with BRUTUS, CATO, STRATO, VOLUMNIUS, and LUCILIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
