<p class="line" name=5.3.97>Where, where, Messala, doth his body lie?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.98>Lo, yonder, and Titinius mourning it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.99>Titinius' face is upward.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>CATO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.100>He is slain.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.101>O Julius Caesar, thou art mighty yet!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.102>Thy spirit walks abroad and turns our swords</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.103>In our own proper entrails.</p>
<p><i>Low alarums</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>CATO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.104>Brave Titinius!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.105>Look, whether he have not crown'd dead Cassius!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.106>Are yet two Romans living such as these?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.107>The last of all the Romans, fare thee well!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.108>It is impossible that ever Rome</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.109>Should breed thy fellow. Friends, I owe more tears</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.110>To this dead man than you shall see me pay.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.111>I shall find time, Cassius, I shall find time.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.112>Come, therefore, and to Thasos send his body:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.113>His funerals shall not be in our camp,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.114>Lest it discomfort us. Lucilius, come;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.115>And come, young Cato; let us to the field.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.116>Labeo and Flavius, set our battles on:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.117>'Tis three o'clock; and, Romans, yet ere night</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.118>We shall try fortune in a second fight.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE IV. Another part of the field.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Alarum. Enter fighting, Soldiers of both armies; then BRUTUS, CATO, LUCILIUS, and others</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.1>Yet, countrymen, O, yet hold up your heads!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>CATO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.2>What bastard doth not? Who will go with me?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.3>I will proclaim my name about the field:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.4>I am the son of Marcus Cato, ho!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.5>A foe to tyrants, and my country's friend;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.6>I am the son of Marcus Cato, ho!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.7>And I am Brutus, Marcus Brutus, I;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.8>Brutus, my country's friend; know me for Brutus!</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>LUCILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.9>O young and noble Cato, art thou down?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.10>Why, now thou diest as bravely as Titinius;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.11>And mayst be honour'd, being Cato's son.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.12>Yield, or thou diest.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>LUCILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.13>Only I yield to die:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.14>There is so much that thou wilt kill me straight;</p>
<p><i>Offering money</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.15>Kill Brutus, and be honour'd in his death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.16>We must not. A noble prisoner!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.17>Room, ho! Tell Antony, Brutus is ta'en.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.18>I'll tell the news. Here comes the general.</p>
<p><i>Enter ANTONY</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.19>Brutus is ta'en, Brutus is ta'en, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.20>Where is he?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>LUCILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.21>Safe, Antony; Brutus is safe enough:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.22>I dare assure thee that no enemy</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.23>Shall ever take alive the noble Brutus:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.24>The gods defend him from so great a shame!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.25>When you do find him, or alive or dead,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.26>He will be found like Brutus, like himself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.27>This is not Brutus, friend; but, I assure you,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.28>A prize no less in worth: keep this man safe;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.29>Give him all kindness: I had rather have</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.30>Such men my friends than enemies. Go on,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.31>And see whether Brutus be alive or dead;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.32>And bring us word unto Octavius' tent</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.33>How every thing is chanced.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE V. Another part of the field.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter BRUTUS, DARDANIUS, CLITUS, STRATO, and VOLUMNIUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.1>Come, poor remains of friends, rest on this rock.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>CLITUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.2>Statilius show'd the torch-light, but, my lord,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.3>He came not back: he is or ta'en or slain.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.4>Sit thee down, Clitus: slaying is the word;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.5>It is a deed in fashion. Hark thee, Clitus.</p>
<p><i>Whispers</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>CLITUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.6>What, I, my lord? No, not for all the world.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.7>Peace then! no words.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>CLITUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.8>I'll rather kill myself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.9>Hark thee, Dardanius.</p>
<p><i>Whispers</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>DARDANIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.10>Shall I do such a deed?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CLITUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.11>O Dardanius!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>DARDANIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.12>O Clitus!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CLITUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.13>What ill request did Brutus make to thee?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>DARDANIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.14>To kill him, Clitus. Look, he meditates.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>CLITUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.15>Now is that noble vessel full of grief,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.16>That it runs over even at his eyes.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.17>Come hither, good Volumnius; list a word.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>VOLUMNIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.18>What says my lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.19>                  Why, this, Volumnius:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.20>The ghost of Caesar hath appear'd to me</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.21>Two several times by night; at Sardis once,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.22>And, this last night, here in Philippi fields:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.23>I know my hour is come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>VOLUMNIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.24>Not so, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.25>Nay, I am sure it is, Volumnius.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.26>Thou seest the world, Volumnius, how it goes;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.27>Our enemies have beat us to the pit:</p>
<p><i>Low alarums</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.28>It is more worthy to leap in ourselves,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.29>Than tarry till they push us. Good Volumnius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.30>Thou know'st that we two went to school together:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.31>Even for that our love of old, I prithee,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.32>Hold thou my sword-hilts, whilst I run on it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>VOLUMNIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.33>That's not an office for a friend, my lord.</p>
<p><i>Alarum still</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>CLITUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.34>Fly, fly, my lord; there is no tarrying here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.35>Farewell to you; and you; and you, Volumnius.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.36>Strato, thou hast been all this while asleep;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.37>Farewell to thee too, Strato. Countrymen,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.38>My heart doth joy that yet in all my life</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.39>I found no man but he was true to me.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.40>I shall have glory by this losing day</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.41>More than Octavius and Mark Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.42>By this vile conquest shall attain unto.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.43>So fare you well at once; for Brutus' tongue</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.44>Hath almost ended his life's history:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.45>Night hangs upon mine eyes; my bones would rest,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.46>That have but labour'd to attain this hour.</p>
<p><i>Alarum. Cry within, 'Fly, fly, fly!'</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>CLITUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.47>Fly, my lord, fly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.48>                  Hence! I will follow.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt CLITUS, DARDANIUS, and VOLUMNIUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.49>I prithee, Strato, stay thou by thy lord:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.50>Thou art a fellow of a good respect;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.51>Thy life hath had some smatch of honour in it:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.52>Hold then my sword, and turn away thy face,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.53>While I do run upon it. Wilt thou, Strato?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>STRATO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.54>Give me your hand first. Fare you well, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.55>Farewell, good Strato.</p>
<p><i>Runs on his sword</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.56>Caesar, now be still:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.57>I kill'd not thee with half so good a will.</p>
<p><i>Dies</i></p>
<p><i>Alarum. Retreat. Enter OCTAVIUS, ANTONY, MESSALA, LUCILIUS, and the army</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.58>What man is that?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.59>My master's man. Strato, where is thy master?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>STRATO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.60>Free from the bondage you are in, Messala:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.61>The conquerors can but make a fire of him;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.62>For Brutus only overcame himself,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.63>And no man else hath honour by his death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>LUCILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.64>So Brutus should be found. I thank thee, Brutus,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.65>That thou hast proved Lucilius' saying true.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.66>All that served Brutus, I will entertain them.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.67>Fellow, wilt thou bestow thy time with me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>STRATO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.68>Ay, if Messala will prefer me to you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.69>Do so, good Messala.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.70>How died my master, Strato?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>STRATO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.71>I held the sword, and he did run on it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>MESSALA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.72>Octavius, then take him to follow thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.73>That did the latest service to my master.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.74>This was the noblest Roman of them all:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.75>All the conspirators save only he</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.76>Did that they did in envy of great Caesar;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.77>He only, in a general honest thought</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.78>And common good to all, made one of them.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.79>His life was gentle, and the elements</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.80>So mix'd in him that Nature might stand up</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.81>And say to all the world 'This was a man!'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>OCTAVIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.82>According to his virtue let us use him,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.83>With all respect and rites of burial.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.84>Within my tent his bones to-night shall lie,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.85>Most like a soldier, order'd honourably.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.86>So call the field to rest; and let's away,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.87>To part the glories of this happy day.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
